Day 1 Grand Prix Washington D.C. Coverage
=========================================



 Posted in **Event Coverage**
 on November 16, 2013 






![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/wizards_author.jpg)
By Wizards of the Coast











![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/closing.jpg)The largest North American Legacy Grand Prix gives way to a pretty large Day 2 field. 235 battle-hardened players escaped from the nearly 1,700 that started the day, including seven players with pristine 9-0 records.


No. 20 Craig Wescoe, Andrew Cuneo, Mike Nyberg, Ted McCluskie, Chas Hinkle, Wayne Polimine, and Rudy Briksza may not be in the Top 8 yet, but an undefeated Day 1 is a pretty good start. Dustin Droggitis and Denis Ulanov also maneuvered through the field with nary a loss, clocking in at 8-0-1.


And though many ranked and well-known names fell by the wayside in the final round, there're plenty of top Pros still in the hunt. No. 10 Sam Black is the highest ranked player left, with No. 13 Eric Froehlich, No. 16 Brian Kibler, No. 22 Owen Turtenwald, and No. 25 Christian Calcano all making the cut as well. Other notable names to make the cut include Chris Pikula, Todd Anderson, Gaudenis Vidugiris, and Tomoharu Saito.


But with a wide-open field, nary a dominant deck to be found, and six rounds in front of us, it's just about anyone's game. Tune in Sunday as we bring you six rounds on the way to the Top 8 and the crowning of the champion of Grand Prix D.C. 2013.


  

[Top 8 Coverage](http://magic.wizards.com/en/events/coverage/gpwdc13)   [Day 2 Coverage](http://magic.wizards.com/en/articles/archive/event-coverage/day-2-grand-prix-washington-dc-coverage-2013-11-17)

---



Saturday, 9:00 a.m. – Interactions to Watch
-------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

 

If you're new to the Legacy format, especially if you've started playing **Magic** in just the last few years, there are going to be some interactions that might get casually mentioned by commentators or in match coverage that could leave you scratching your head and calling up [Gatherer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Default.aspx). And some rules interactions for cards printed sometimes more than a decade apart can be confusing enough that even the Oracle text won't clean it up for you.


But that's why we're here. While we can't explain every single interaction to you, we can highlight some of the more common ones, talk about how they interact, and any rules quirks that might be involved.


### [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell)/Giant creature/Enters the battlefield effects


This might be the most common sight this weekend, if recent trends hold. [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) is a "balanced" card in that it lets both players put something into play. But because one player built their deck with it in mind, that usually a less than fair exchange. Dropping [Batterskull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterskull) into play isn't nearly as exciting as [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) crashing onto the battlefield.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Show and Tell
 | 
Emrakul, the Aeons Torn
 |

First, the way [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) works is that both players select their card (by setting it aside or otherwise indicating which one they've selected) before they are revealed. This means both players have to make their decision without knowing what card their opponent is choosing.


Some players fight [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) with creatures that enter the battlefield with an effect, such as [Bone Shredder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bone+Shredder) or [Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake). In these cases, both cards are in play when the effect goes on the stack, so the following interaction can happen...


### [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn)/[Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas)/[Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake)


If [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) puts [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) and a [Bone Shredder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bone+Shredder) into play, the [Bone Shredder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bone+Shredder) will kill the normally nigh-unkillable [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn). Why? Because [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn)'s protection only extends to spells. Once a creature is in play, it's now a permanent and no longer a spell, meaning it's free to use its effect to target the Eldrazi. Same goes for [Gilded Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gilded+Drake).


[Karakas](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karakas) works similarly. It's neither a spell nor does it have a color, so it is free to target [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Emrakul%252C%2Bthe%2BAeons%2BTorn).


### [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/[Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) or [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)


This one is relatively simple compared to others on the list. Player A casts a spell. Player B has [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) and [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). When Player A casts his or her spell, Player B gets a triggered ability for [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance). In response, Player B can then use [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) or [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) to rearrange the top of his or her library to get the right card in place, then let the trigger resolve and (likely) counter the spell. If the spell costs one mana, in a pinch, Top itself can be activated to go on top of the library.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Counterbalance
 | 
Sensei's Divining Top
 |

Note that split second, particularly [Krosan Grip](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krosan+Grip), freezes this line of play out. [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) still triggers, but Player B cannot activate [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top). For this reason, it is sometimes advisable to keep a card that costs three on top of your library for just such an instance.


That trick doesn't even work against [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay), which says right on the card that it can't be countered. It doesn't matter what [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) reveals...it will resolve (same for [Loxodon Smiter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loxodon+Smiter), [Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Supreme+Verdict), etc.).


### [Helm of Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Helm+of+Obedience)/[Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace)


[Helm of Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Helm+of+Obedience)'s purpose is to mill your opponent until you've milled X cards or a creature, and then you get that creature. Basically, it was meant to be [Control Magic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Control+Magic) for a random library creature or a faster [Millstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Millstone) against players with no creatures (a common strategy when Helm was originally printed). However, for Helm to stop milling, it requires a card actually go to the graveyard. [Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace) (and [Leyline of the Void](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+the+Void)) makes sure no card ever hits the graveyard, and thus Helm never stops milling. As a result, the entire deck is exiled and the milled player generally loses on their next draw step.


### [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond)/[Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor)


[Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond) confuses a lot of new players. "Why would I want to discard my hand to get mana?" they often ask. "I can't even use the mana to cast my spells anymore!"


The trick with [Lion's Eye Diamond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lion%27s+Eye+Diamond) is to either A) Play cards from your graveyard or want to discard (like Dredge does) or B) play it in response to a card that puts other cards in your hand.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Lion's Eye Diamond
 | 
Infernal Tutor
 |

[Infernal Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Infernal+Tutor) is the poster child for B), as not only is it placing any card in your hand (say, a [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames)?), but it actually wants your hand to be empty when doing so, making these two a lethal combination.


### [Punishing Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punishing+Fire)/[Grove of the Burnwillows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Burnwillows)


This one is pretty simple. [Grove of the Burnwillows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Burnwillows) gives opponents life on demand and, as luck would have it, pays to return [Punishing Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punishing+Fire). Managing the triggers against [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman), however, can be tricky. And when there are multiple Groves and multiple Deathrites (unlikely, since they die to [Punishing Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punishing+Fire)), things can get complicated. Just know that Fire doesn't return until the trigger resolves and neither does [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) (or [Scavenging Ooze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scavenging+Ooze)).


### [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe)/[Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy)


[Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) used to be a guessing game, but now Storm decks are packing these two cards to get a leg-up on decision making. "Blind" Therapies—casting [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) with no knowledge of their hand—have become less common since [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) was printed.


### [Shardless Agent](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shardless+Agent)/[Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)


This works exactly like you'd like it to. Normally, [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision) has to be suspended, but if you cascade into it, you can cast it normally. And since its nonexistent cost is read as "0" for the purposes of Cascade (and things like [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)), it will always get cast if it's the first spell hit by Shardless Agent.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Shardless Agent
 | 
Ancestral Vision
 |

This is the same principle that lets Cascade spells cast [Living Death](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Living+Death) in Modern.


### [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature)/[Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid)/[Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel)/[Birchlore Rangers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birchlore+Rangers)


The key card to this chain is [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel), which untaps with every Green spell cast. With Birchlore Ranger or [Heritage Druid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heritage+Druid), you can tap [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel) and one or two more elves to make mana, letting you cast another Green creature and untap [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel). If you've already cast [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature), this lets you also draw a card, meaning every card usually nets you more cards and either more mana or breaking even on mana. The combo works best with multiple [Nettle Sentinel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nettle+Sentinel)s.


### [Painter's Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Painter%27s+Servant)/[Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone)


Similar in execution to [Helm of Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Helm+of+Obedience)/[Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace), this combination mills out an entirely library when cast, with some complications.


The basis of the combo is that [Painter's Servant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Painter%27s+Servant) makes all cards one color, even in the library, so [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone)'s "do this again" clause is always met.


Where things get tricky is when a player has either [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) or an Eldrazi (or something like [Gaea's Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Blessing)) in the deck. Eldrazi have triggered abilities that won't go on the stack until [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone) is done resolving (i.e., the deck is empty). The result will be that the entire deck will get reshuffled, undoing everything the [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone) player did.


[Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), however, has a replacement effect, meaning that it gets shuffled back in while [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone) is doing its thing. Barring anything else, this usually means one of two things. 1) If there's only one [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), that card ends up as the last card left in the deck, and that card only 2) If there are multiple [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus), the game will end in a tie with an unresolvable loop, as [Grindstone](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grindstone) will continually hit two [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) that immediately are shuffled back in.


### Killing [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis)


[True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis) isn't completely unkillable, though it's close. If it's the only creature on the board, [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) will force its controller to sacrifice it, since it doesn't target or deal damage to [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis). [Supreme Verdict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Supreme+Verdict) also kills it, as would [Celestial Flare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Flare) if it's the only attacking creature. New Commander addition [Toxic Deluge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toxic+Deluge) will also do it, as would [Massacre](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Massacre) or any other untargeted way of shrinking its power and toughness.


Remember, "DEBT" to remember what protection stops: Damage, Enchanted (or Equipped), Blocking, Targeting. Any other way of killing [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis) is fare game.


### Humility/Creatures


I don't know. Ask a judge.




---



Saturday, 9:15 a.m. – A Comprehensive Guide to the Decks of Legacy
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

 

When players talk about diverse formats, they're usually referring to a format where five or maybe even six archetypes are viable and no one strategy dominates. If you stretch that into viable variations of archetypes, sometimes you'll see as many as eight or nine decks make waves at one time or another, similar to how Standard is right now.


Legacy right now has somewhere around 20 viable archetypes, depending on how you define viable. That wasn't a type. Twenty. 20. Zwanzig. Viente. Vingt. There are 22 (zweiundzwanzig, for you German speakers out there) in this article alone, and I've left out decks that have Top 8'd Grand Prix (apologizes to No. 10 Sam Black and [Goblin Bombardment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bombardment)).


In other words, Legacy is diverse.


In fact, Legacy might be the most diverse format on the planet, short of Commander or the kitchen tables around the world where anything goes.


With 22 decks, I really can't waste this many words on an introduction, let alone counting lessons in foreign languages. Let's get to it. You can read on for the whole picture of the Legacy format, or click on any deck name here to get the full description below.


* [Sneak and Show](#sneak)
* [Death and Taxes](#death)
* [Delver decks](#delver)
* [Ad Nauseam Tendrils/Storm](#ad)
* [UWx Counterbalance Top](#uwx)
* [Reanimator](#reanimator)
* [Shardless BUG](#shardless)
* [Esper Stoneblade](#esper)
* [Jund](#jund)
* [Bant](#bant)
* [Elves](#elves)
* [Dredge](#dredge)
* [Merfolk](#merfolk)
* [Everything else](#everything)


### Sneak and Show


Sneak and Show is the deck de jour in Legacy at the moment, and it's easy to see why. Using [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack) and [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) to throw down [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) and [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) lightning quick, the two-color deck is fast, consistent, and can play all of the important Blue cards, particularly [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will). Expect players to show up in droves with the deck, especially after William Jensen's twin 2nd place finishes at SCG Open Los Angeles and the SCG Invitational.








#### Sneak and Show—William Jensen

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Misty+Rainforest)



















### Death and Taxes


Death and Taxes isn't the most popular deck, but it's certainly on everyone's radar after Ari Lax dropped his beloved Tendrils deck and picked up this Mono White deck on his way to the 2013 Legacy Championship.


Yes, a White Weenie deck is a viable choice in a format with [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), and potential turn 1-2 kills.


At its core, Death and Taxes is a disruption deck, attacking players' mana ([Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), [Rishadan Port](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rishadan+Port), [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben)) and presenting creatures that keep a number of Legacy decks unbalanced and unable to execute their gameplan ([Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor), [Phyrexian Revoker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Revoker)) before finishing them off with a few of the format's more dangerous creatures. If you've never attacked with a [Mirran Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mirran+Crusader) equiped with an [Umezawa's Jitte](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Umezawa%27s+Jitte) or [Sword of Fire and Ice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sword+of+Fire+and+Ice) (or both!), you don't know what you're missing.








#### Death and Taxes—Ari Lax, Legacy Championship, 1st


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Delver (UR, URW, RUG)


There are a variety of ways to build around [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), but all of them involve cheap (or free) countermagic, [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland), low land counts, and the ever present [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm). Where you go from there is often a matter of taste.


RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) has traditionally been the most popular, as [Nimble Mongoose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimble+Mongoose) and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) provide potentially giant, difficult to handle threats for very little investment, while [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) increases a clock and clears out pesky creatures. Absolutely nothing in the main deck costs more than two mana, typically, and the deck thrives on keeping both players low on mana.


Recently, however, players have come out from under RUG and experimented with other colors to pair with their [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)s and Bolts. Osyp Lebedowicz took second at the Legacy Championships with straight UR [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets), supplementing the Red-Blue core with relative newcomers [Young Pyromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Young+Pyromancer) and [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis). For his efforts, he gains [Blood Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Moon) in the sideboard and better resistance to [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland).


Others have opted for UWR Devler, a slightly more controlling version that plays [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares) and [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic)s alongside heavy-hitter [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft).








#### RUG Delver—Ricky Sidher, SCG Open Los Angeles, 1st

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Misty+Rainforest)



















### Ad Nauseam Tendrils/Storm


There are various options for casting a lot of spells very quickly and very early to win the game, but [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) Tendrils is the most common you'll see in Legacy. The deck plays a ton of "rituals"—cards that make more mana than they cost, like namesake [Dark Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Ritual) and successor [Cabal Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Ritual)—and deck manipulation to cast a lot of spells before finishing with a lethal [Tendrils of Agony](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tendrils+of+Agony). [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) and [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) usually give the deck the extra kick it needs to hit enough spells in a single turn to win.


The deck can win as early as turn one, though that's rare. It's more likely to clear the way with [Duress](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duress) and [Cabal Therapy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cabal+Therapy) before winning sometime on or before turn four.








#### Ad Nauseam Tendrils—Mark Tocco, Legacy Championships Top 8

### UWx Counterbalance/Top


[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/[Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) has been a combo that has been potent against Legacy's low mana curves for quite some time, but really got a push when *Avacyn Restored* gave the world the Miracle mechanic, generally, and [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus) specifically.


Between [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm) and [Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top)—not to mention [Enlightened Tutor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Enlightened+Tutor)—the Blue-White based [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) decks have near absolute control over what's on top of their deck, letting them set up the [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) lock against combo decks or getting incredibly cheap board sweepers against aggressive decks. [Entreat the Angels](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entreat+the+Angels) is often a finisher, though players have also recently adapted the [Helm of Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Helm+of+Obedience)/[Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace) kill as well.


[Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) has hurt the deck significantly, but clearly has not pushed it completely out of the format.








#### UWR Miracles—Paul Lynch, Legacy Championships, Top 8

### Reanimator


When [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) was first spoiled, everyone expected Reanimator to run rampant over the format, destroying people Turn 1 Necro-style left and right.


That didn't quite come to pass—in fact, not a single copy made the Top 8 at its debut tournament in Grand Prix Atlanta in 2012—but Reanimator is still a powerful strategy thanks to [Exhume](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Exhume), [Reanimate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reanimate), and [Entomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Entomb). [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) helps keep the strategy in check, but the little 1/2 that could hasn't been enough to completely remove it from the format.


Reanimator has also recently adopted [Tidespout Tyrant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tidespout+Tyrant) as a way to utilize its plethora of cheap spells after it has achieved its "combo."








#### Reanimator—Robert Cucanto, SCG Open Indianapolis, Top 8


##### 






![Download Arena Decklist](https://web.archive.org/web/20211024134741im_/https://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download_arena.png)
![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Shardless BUG


The dark and [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets)-less cousin to RUG, Shardless BUG plays a disruptive game that attacks the hand instead of the mana base. [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach), [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) and [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) keep hand sizes down, while [Ancestral Vision](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancestral+Vision)s, Shardless Agent and [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) keep its own hand size flush. Fellow Commander standout [Baleful Strix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Baleful+Strix) offers utility, and [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) does pretty much everything. Plus, the deck gets to play format all-star [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) in its main deck.








#### Shardless BUG—Camden Atkins, SCG Invitational, 3rd Place


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Esper Stoneblade


Esper Stoneblade has occasionally held the title of the best and/or most popular deck in the format. It is, at its heart, a [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm)/[Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will) deck that uses counters and discard to keep opponents off-balance while [Stoneforge Mystic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stoneforge+Mystic) finds powerful equipment to kill quickly. The deck used to play [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls)—thanks in no small part to No. 9 Tom Martell's success with that card in the deck—but recently players have been abandoning it for [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis), which holds equipment just as well, if not better.








#### Esper Stoneblade—Mark Ivazaj, SCG Open Los Angeles


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Creeping+Tar+Pit)



















### Jund


Ah, Jund. Good old Jund. Viable in every format ever, except maybe Vintage. Jund doesn't get to play [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), but it does get to play a lot of efficient, disruptive cards. It even closely resembles the Modern version of Jund prior to the banning of [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf). [Hymn to Tourach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hymn+to+Tourach) and the [Punishing Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punishing+Fire)/[Grove of the Burnwillows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Burnwillows) combo are the main differentiators, but otherwise it's a very similar concept to the Jund decks we've all come to love/loathe over the years.








#### Jund—Vidianto Wijaya, SCG Open Los Angeles, 3rd Place

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)



















### Bant


Bant doesn't get a ton of attention or play just yet, but that could certainly change after No. 10 Reid Duke won an SCG Open with it. Duke isn't the first to combine GW [Knight of the Reliquary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+the+Reliquary) decks with Blue cards, but his win represents the most recent revival of the strategy.








#### Bant—Reid Duke, SCG Open Indianapolis, 1st


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)



















### Elves


Part creature deck, part combo deck, Elves is a unique deck in the format. The linear tribal strategy can play for quick beatdowns with a plethora of quick creatures, it can combo off with [Glimpse of Nature](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glimpse+of+Nature) and various mana-producing elves, and it can go positively huge with [Natural Order](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Natural+Order) for [Craterhoof Behemoth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Craterhoof+Behemoth), [Regal Force](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Regal+Force), or [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus). While it's weak to [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance), [Engineered Explosives](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Engineered+Explosives), and more, it's also the deck best equipped to take advantage of [Gaea's Cradle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaea%27s+Cradle), a card that is not inaccurately described as the Green [Tolarian Academy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tolarian+Academy).








#### Elves—Chris Anderson, SCG Open Indianapolis, Top 8

### Dredge


Dredge has been a boogeyman of formats past, but has become less-so as graveyard hate becomes more prevalent. [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman), [Scavenging Ooze](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scavenging+Ooze), and even [Rest in Peace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rest+in+Peace) all see main deck play, and sideboards usually have even more ways to attack graveyards. Still, Dredge is deadly enough that if people don't come prepared to fight positively packed graveyards, it can do some dirty, dirty things.








#### Dredge, Andrew Dziedzic, SCG Open Milwaukee, Top 8


##### 






![Download Arena Decklist](https://web.archive.org/web/20211024134741im_/https://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download_arena.png)
![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Merfolk


Merfolk has, at times, been one of, if not the, best decks in the format. However, metagame shifts and new cards have drowned out the previously unsinkable fish men and women. [Punishing Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Punishing+Fire), [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay), [Terminus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminus), and more have slowly, but surely, churned the format up enough that Merfolk can't simply be penciled in for a Top 8 anymore.


However, the deck has some characteristics that make it occasionally good. It's [Wasteland](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wasteland) resistant while playing its own, it has disruptive elements, and a relatively fast clock for an attacking deck. And now it also gets to play [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis)—which just happens to be a Merfolk.








#### Merfolk—Alexander Dochnal, SCG Dallas, Top 8

### Everything else


Legacy has such a wide variety of options, that it's virtually impossible to list all of the archetypes we might see here this weekend. While the tier one and tier two decks are relatively settled, Legacy has a large enough cardpool that innovation can be rewarding. Sam Black, for example, sacrificed his way to a Top 8 at [GP Atlanta](/en/events/coverage/vidugiris-wins-third-grand-prix-title) with a Goblin-Bombardment/[Blood Artist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Artist) brew that never caught on. Likewise, Caleb Durward—who invented the [Survival of the Fittest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Survival+of+the+Fittest)/[Vengevine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vengevine) deck that broke Legacy in half several years back—has long been a proponent of a Black-Green deck called "Nic Fit" that uses a lot of basic lands and [Veteran Explorer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Veteran+Explorer) to attack the format from a different angle.


Still, here are a number of decks that, though they don't command much attention, do pop up now and then.








#### MUD—Greg Price, Legacy Championships, Top 8

Saturday, 9:30 a.m. – More Than a True-Name
-------------------------------------------


*by Adam Styborski*

  
The Grand Prix is just underway here outside D.C. and there's one card on the tip of everyone's tongue: [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis).



![True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=True-Name+Nemesis)

The standout Merfolk from the recent Grixis-themed Commander release found plenty of room for itself in Legacy. [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) decks of every sort have added the three-drop, including Osyp Lebedowicz's 2013 Legacy Championship runner up deck. Those who choose the less-common tribal Merfolk route have adopted the difficult-to-kill kinsman as well. But there's much more to what players want than the nemesis of their opponents.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/dealers.jpg)
The next most request cards across several dealers on site were more Commander (2013 Edition) additions to the format: [Toxic Deluge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toxic+Deluge) and Swansong.




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Toxic Deluge
 | 
Swan Song
 |

Non-Commander release cards requested included [Cataclysm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cataclysm), [Xantid Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xantid+Swarm), [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim), and Flusterstorm. What all these cards have in common is that they serve very specific purposes. Swansong is a cheap counterspell that can handle popular combo deck Sneak and Show. [Toxic Deluge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Toxic+Deluge) can wipe away the disruptive creatures in Death and Taxes, and reset the board for creature-based combos like Elves. It also neatly deals with normally difficult creatures like [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis). [Xantid Swarm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Xantid+Swarm) helps *protect* combos going off in the same way Flusterstorm specially answers Storm and [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) Tendrils. Cheap, flexible answers like [Nature's Claim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nature%27s+Claim) are the archetypical options outside of the maindecks in Legacy.


Perhaps the most intriguing tidbit came from one dealer who wished they had brought copies of [Envelop](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Envelop), requested "by some key people." It isn't difficult to believe it's another specific card to be included in sideboards, meant for specific decks throughout the weekend. Who these players were remains a mystery, but we'll be keeping an eye out to find an answer.




---

  
  

 

Saturday, 12:00 p.m. – Players to Watch
---------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

  
Legacy is a different animal. Including cards from as far back as Alpha, Legacy offers possibly the most diverse, most open, format available. It also only gets played at a high level a few times a year, meaning that even the best players in the world may not necessarily be among the best Legacy players in the world.


But there are plenty of players who not only dedicate time to the format, but have shown time and time again their ability to adapt to and advance through the Legacy metagame. So while it doesn't take much analysis to tell you that you should probably keep an eye on 2nd-ranked Josh Utter-Leyton, we did comb through the players in attendance to pluck out those with particular experience and success in Legacy. These are a few of those players to watch.


### No. 3 Reid Duke


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/wc13/Reid-Duke_portrait_2013.jpg)
Ranked 3rd in the world, picking Reid Duke as a player to watch is a little like saying "Hey, you should watch out for that Lebron James guy. I hear he's good."


Duke is a threat to win, place, or show at any tournament he comes prepared for, and based on his recent win at the SCG Legacy Open in Indianapolis, he seems plenty prepared for the format. Piloting a Bant deck that hasn't been played much--if at all--in recent months, Duke picked his spot and poked at the metagame a bit on his way to yet another Legacy Open win.


What makes Duke such a threat is his versatility. He won another Legacy Open a few months back in Philadelphia with Elves, a completely different style of deck from his Bant list. I've also seen him pilot Top/[Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance) lists and have success with other archetypes. Given his close friendship with teammate William Jensen (see below), it's likely Duke knows the popular and powerful Sneak and Show deck inside and out as well.


Given all of this, I'd be more surprised to see Duke miss Day 2 than almost anyone else in the field.


### No. 10 Sam Black


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/ptths13/black1.jpg)
Whether we're watching 10th-ranked Sam Black for his overall skill level (hint: world class) or his penchant for building new, seemingly odd decks in Legacy (fairly high), you can rest assured we'll be keeping an eye on the innovative deckbuilder all weekend.


This was particularly on display back in 2012 at GP Atlanta, where Black took a RWB sacrifice deck to a Top 8 despite what, on paper, looked like a lackluster collection of cards. The synergy Black found, however, was enough to push the deck over the top. Since then, the strategy has virtually disappeared nearly as fast as it appeared in the first place.


### Ari Lax


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/eternal13/trophy.jpg)
If Ari Lax were merely the 2013 Legacy Champion, he'd earn his spot on this list. But Lax is much more than that. A long-time leader in the Legacy format, and a champion of the [Ad Nauseam](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ad+Nauseam) Tendrils (ANT) deck, Lax has served as a voice for the format and one of the true masters of the metagame. Even when Legacy isn't on the minds of most players, you can read about the ebbs and flows in the format on an almost weekly basis from Ari. And all of that work paid off this year when Lax set aside his pet ANT deck and won the Legacy Championship with...White Weenie?


Basically the antithesis of Lax's pet combo deck, the Legacy champ proved his flexibility by switching to Death and Taxes when he deemed it appropriate and was handsomely rewarded. It will be interesting to see if Lax sticks to playing the Basic Plains that earned him the crown, or moves back to the deck that he's championed for so long.


### William Jensen


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/magazine/events/halloffame/2013/jensen_5.jpg)
Ever since re-entering the game last year, newly crowned Hall of Famer William Jensen has staked his claim as a player to watch. One of the game's true old guard, and now firmly re-established as one of the best in the world once again, Jensen has showed he can handle Legacy as easily as he's been breezing through Standard and Limited as of late. He took second at the SCG Invitational—which was part Standard, part Legacy—and showed that wasn't a fluke with a second runner-up finish at SCG Los Angeles. He was piloting Sneak and Show at both tournaments, but that deck has had a target painted on its back in large part because of how Jensen has finished. The strength of that deck might be gauged simply by whether Jensen has opted to run it back for a third time.


### Gaudenis Vidugiris


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpatl12/Winner620.JPG)
Gaudenis Vidugiris is one of the most dangerous players around and someone I keep an eye on personally every time I do coverage. Part of the reason I always pay attention is that I was there at GP Atlanta when Vidugiris won the whole thing after virtually audibling into his deck (and out of Sam Black's). He even had booked an early flight that he had to run to as soon as the Top 8 was finished, not actually expecting to do as well as he did. Vidugiris is a naturally adept magician and has shown his ability to win an entire Legacy GP. It would shock no one if he did it again.


### Osyp Lebedowicz


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/eternal13/Osyp.jpg)
Osyp Lebedowicz is another longtime player who seems to have a penchant for Legacy. He recently took second at the 2013 Legacy Championship with UR [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) and has excelled in older formats. The former Pro Tour winner doesn't have any Legacy GP Top 8s to his name, but it wouldn't be shocking to see him finally claim one in D.C.


### Jacob Wilson


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpstr13/t8_wilson.jpg)
One of the cool things about Eternal formats like Legacy is that you can often play the same deck for a long time. Jacob Wilson is one player who has taken advantage of that, winning the SCG Legacy Open in Seattle with RUG [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) as well as earning a GP Top 8 last April in Strasburg with the same exact archetype. Wilson has a penchant for performing at the Grand Prix Level, so keep an eye on him as the weekend progresses.




---

  
  

 

Saturday, 2:30 p.m. – Things To Do in Legacy for Fun and Profit
---------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*

  
A lot of the press for Legacy goes, rightfully so, to the heavy hitting, spikiest of Spike cards like [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), [Brainstorm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brainstorm), [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell), and other cards that aren't Blue.


But as the most diverse format with the largest non-Vintage cardpool, a lot of crazy, interesting stuff happens. Since you aren't here to see all of the sweetness, we're more than happy to bring some snapshots right to your computer (you're welcome).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Kobolds.jpg)  
*Kobolds*
Why start you off slow? Look at this insanity. Three Kobolds, two [Phyrexian Walker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Walker)s, and one very important [Signal Pest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Signal+Pest). Oh, and this was turn two. You see, the Kobold lord playing this deck removed an [Elvish Spirit Guide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elvish+Spirit+Guide) to power out the Pest, and relied on the zeroes in the upper right hand corners of the other cards to start getting in for chunks of damage immediately.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/True-Name.jpg)  
*[True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis)*
Gearing back down for a moment, this should prove to be a common sight over the course of the weekend, as [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis) attacks past...[True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis). These Nemeses showdowns are, as in this picture, often going to be decided by who can enhance their Merfolk [Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Progenitus) with Equipment to turn the tide.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Metalworker.jpg)  
*[Metalworker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metalworker)*
[Metalworker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metalworker) doesn't get nearly enough love in Legacy. Once one of the most feared cards around, you don't see it much anymore these days, in part due to the ubiquity of [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt), [Swords to Plowshares](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swords+to+Plowshares), [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember), and other spot removal. But when it gets doing, well, this happens.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Goblins%20Mirror.jpg)  
*Goblins* 
One of the reasons people love Legacy is that it has a strong Tribal component. It's the one format where you can see two players battling in a Goblins Mirror and not immediately write them off. Plus, how in the world does one actually beat [Krenko, Mob Boss](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Krenko%2C+Mob+Boss) and [Siege-Gang Commander](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Siege-Gang+Commander)? Is that even possible?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Slivers.jpg)  
*Slivers* 
Speaking of tribes, Slivers! Counter Sliver used to be one of the most impressive decks in the old Extended format, and some players have chosen to port the tribe over to Legacy. Given their recent return in ***Magic** 2014*, it's not surprise to see some players trying out some of the new additions. There are more than a few players who picked up the deck, including one who won a Grinder on Friday (the deck list wasn't available for the Grinder roundup. Suffice to say it was Slivers, [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember)s, and [Æther Vial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=%C3%86ther+Vial)s).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/High%20Tide.jpg)  
*[High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide)*
Once one of the most feared decks in Legacy thanks to the legacy of the Hatfield brothers, [High Tide](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=High+Tide) has fallen by the wayside lately. That doesn't mean it isn't something to watch out for. See those dice? They represent the amount of mana in the Mono Blue player's mana pool. Yeah, that [Kira, Great Glass-Spinner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kira%2C+Great+Glass-Spinner) isn't going to do much.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Birthing%20Pod.jpg)  
*[Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod)*
[Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod): It's not just for Modern anymore! A Legacy [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) deck has been popping up lately, chaining all kinds of value creatures into, well, other value creatures. The chain continues all the way up to Titans of the Grave and Primeval variety.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Dredge.jpg)  
*Dredge* 
This is your regular public service reminder that Dredge is a deck and you can leave your graveyard hate at home to your own peril. This isn't someone spreading out their deck—that's their graveyard above the [Gemstone Mine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gemstone+Mine)s.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpwas13/Depths.jpg)  
*[Dark Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Depths)*
When the Legend rule was changed to its current form, it opened up a few more combos, the most notable of which was the [Thespian's Stage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thespian%27s+Stage)/[Dark Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Depths) combo that lets a player copy [Dark Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Depths) with Stage, keep the Stage in play, and immediately make a 20/20, since the new Stage/Depths has no counters on it. This player was ready for almost anything with both Not of this World and [Fling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fling) at the ready to go lethal with his indestructible monster, but his opponent was ready as well—with [Stifle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stifle) for the trigger that would have created the 20/20.




---

  
  

 

Saturday, 3:00 p.m. – All Lines Lead to the DC Metagame
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Adam Styborski*

  
When you want to talk about "the Legacy metagame" you have to take a step back. Well over 10,000 cards grants players access to nearly any deck their heart desires, leading to the format's legendary diversity. While there are frequent large tournaments sharing results, there isn't nearly the mass of events like those for Standard and Modern.


Legacy sits out alone, but there are some guideposts to point the way.


The [2013 Legacy Championship](/en/articles/archive/event-coverage/legacy-coverage-eternal-championships-2013-2013-11-02) at [Eternal Weekend](/en/events/coverage/lims-fish-reel-deal-philly) is the most recent sign. Ari Lax's victory with the disruptive Death and Taxes deck firmly put monowhite as one road in.








#### Death and Taxes - Ari Lax, Winner 2013 Legacy Championship

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Karakas)


















"I mean, I wouldn't call this deck fair," Lax said about his choice for the weekend. With access to the best dual lands in **Magic**'s history it can be surprising to see just one color at work, but it's the army of creature-answers like [Phyrexian Revoker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phyrexian+Revoker), [Mangara of Corondor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mangara+of+Corondor), and [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben) that can make life difficult for whatever opponents are planning.


Also featured in the finals was Osyp Lebedowicz playing a blue-red [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) deck. Having lands other than the ubiquitous duals is something every deck needs to consider. "Being able to fetch out a first-turn basic Island is so good in many of the matchups here," Lebedowicz said. Having a little mane goes a long way for [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Delver%2Bof%2BSecrets) decks.








#### U/R Delver - Osyp Lebedowicz, 2nd 2013 Legacy Championship

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wasteland)


















While creatures like [Young Pyromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Young+Pyromancer) and [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis) don't shut down opponents, they do a great job ignoring whatever the enemy tries while applying pressure to life totals. Big decks with small creatures might seem strange for Legacy. Where are all the combo decks?


The StarCityGames Invitational a month ago featured a mirror match finals of Sneak and Show decks between winner Brad Nelson and Pro Tour Hall of Famer William "Huey" Jensen.








#### Sneak and Show - Brad Nelson, Winner 2013 StarCityGames Invitational Indianapolis

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Misty+Rainforest)


















There are no small fries here. Ordinarily nigh uncastable [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) and [Emrakul, the Aeons Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeons+Torn) are easily slipped into play thanks to [Show and Tell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Show+and+Tell) or [Sneak Attack](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sneak+Attack), the deck's namesake combo pieces. With the best card filtering and mana acceleration in the format, games can end before anything else ever happens.


Not all combo decks were laid out near Washington, D.C. either. Across the pond at the Legacy Bazaar of Moxen two weeks ago, 2013 World Champion and the 4th ranked player in the world Shahar Shenhar played Death and Taxes to a runner up place against winner Julian Knab's Elves.








#### Elves - Julian Knab, Winner 2013 Legacy Bazaar of Moxen


#####

![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)
